# Backlog

WSJF-prioritized 🟡 follow-ups across the project. Single source of truth for "small things that didn't block locking but need to land before phase close."

## Methodology

Each item gets:
- **Cost of Delay (COD)**: 1-5 (5 = waiting hurts a lot; 1 = waiting is harmless)
- **Job Size (JS)**: 1-5 (5 = days; 1 = minutes)
- **WSJF priority**: COD ÷ JS (higher = do sooner)

**Main table sort**: by B-ID (insertion-event order, NOT strictly monotonic-by-number). During the Round 3 D72 deep validation cycle, B-numbers were added in batches and inserted at the anchor of the prior closing batch, causing B53-B73 to appear before B38-B50 in the table. The ID itself remains strictly monotonic (every B-number unique and assigned in order of issuance); the table ordering merely reflects when each batch was appended. **B74 tracks the optional re-sort to strict-monotonic-by-B-ID view** (low priority — not load-bearing for any downstream reader). For WSJF-priority view, see "High / Medium / Lower priority" sections below.

**WSJF policy**: update WSJF when scope or context changes; never re-sort silently — log the change.

**Status-render convention** (clarified 2026-05-11 per Pattern F unscoped audit finding):

When a B-item entry shows a leading status badge (e.g., `(🟡 Open)`) AND an inline `**CLOSED YYYY-MM-DD**` annotation in the same row, **the inline annotation is the authoritative status**. The leading badge is sometimes left stale during round close-out when the producer adds the closure annotation inline rather than flipping the badge. This is a known render-discipline gap tracked as B144 (candidate Pitfall #9 sub-class 9.j — B-item status-render discipline) for Round 7 close-out cleanup. Until then, readers should consult inline annotations + the "Closed in Round N" sections (e.g., L242+ for Round 6 closures) as the canonical view, not the leading badge alone.

## How items get added

Two paths:

1. **Validation log → Backlog**: when a `_validation_log.md` entry has 🟡 follow-ups, those items get B-numbers and land here.
2. **Phase deliverable → Backlog**: open Phase deliverables (especially Phase 0's 0.X items that are still ⬜) become B-numbered when they're worked on.

Process:
1. Add row at end of table with next available `B<N>` ID
2. Score COD and JS
3. Compute WSJF
4. Re-sort if needed (or just append; the priority table is the sorted view)
5. Reference the source (validation log entry, phase deliverable, decision)

## How items leave the backlog

When an item is completed:
1. Close it in `CURRENT_STATE.md` "Recently completed" section
2. Add a row in this table's "Completed" section (below) with completion date and reference to the change
3. Don't delete the row — append-only audit trail

## Source-exact Parquet redesign brainstorm cohort items B-353-B-373 — added 2026-05-17 per 3-agent gap-check (design-reviewer `a472e0575d28816bb` + researcher `a54fcc995f87f919c` + gap-check `afad0935ac58cd263`)

Plan source: `docs/migration/UDM_PIPELINE_REDESIGN_PARQUET_SOURCE_EXACT_2026-05-17.md` (DRAFT v1; SUPERSEDED by Phase A/B split per pipeline-lead direction 2026-05-17 "Proceed with your recommended next steps + log the issues found"). Research grounding: `docs/migration/_research/r6-pme-extraction-time-2026-05-17.md`.

- **B-353** (🟡 Open; **CRITICAL**; WSJF 5.0): **Confirm pyarrow PME availability on RHEL** target environment. pyarrow PME requires `parquet-encryption` CMake compile flag; NOT in stock PyPI wheel pre-pyarrow-15.x. Spike: pip install on RHEL test box → verify `from pyarrow.parquet import encryption` imports without error → test write+read round-trip with PME. Document wheel-provenance requirement in `requirements.txt` or system package spec. **Gate-blocker for D-NEW-B (PME) lock**; gates Phase B. Phase A does NOT depend on PME. Full context: `_research/r6-pme-extraction-time-2026-05-17.md` R2-1. Closure target: BEFORE Phase B kick-off. Source: design-reviewer + researcher convergence 2026-05-17.

- **B-354** (🟡 Open; **CRITICAL**; WSJF 1.67): **Redesign PME column-key granularity model in plan §4.2** — plan pseudocode `column_keys={"SSN": "subject_key_id_for_ssn_row"}` is misleading; PME's `column_keys` is per-column file-scoped, NOT per-row. Per-subject granularity is implemented by KmsClient resolution (key ID is a label, KmsClient resolves to actual key material via PiiSubjectKeys lookup). Document this layer-of-indirection explicitly. Choose between: (a) per-file column key (batch-level shredding); (b) row-group-per-subject layout (operationally complex; violates D45.2 sort); (c) accept KmsClient-resolved per-subject via key-ID encoding. **Gate-blocker for D-NEW-B lock**; Phase B scope. Full context: `_research/r6-pme-extraction-time-2026-05-17.md` R2-5 + design-reviewer Section B2. Source: design-reviewer + researcher convergence 2026-05-17.

- **B-355** (🟡 Open; **CRITICAL**; WSJF 1.33): **Design and specify `PyArrowKmsClient` bridge** between TPM2-sealed master KEK and pyarrow's `KmsClient` interface (`wrap_key` / `unwrap_key` per RFC 3394). pyarrow PME does NOT ship reference KMS client; we must implement. Architecture (per `_research/r6-pme-extraction-time-2026-05-17.md` R3-3): (1) startup unseal master KEK from TPM2; (2) per-subject DEK lookup from `PiiSubjectKeys` (batched); (3) AES-GCM unwrap in-memory; (4) zero master KEK on exit. **Gate-blocker for D-NEW-B lock**; Phase B scope. Source: design-reviewer + researcher convergence 2026-05-17.

- **B-356** (🟡 Open; **CRITICAL**; WSJF 2.5): **Revise D-NEW-D extraction-timestamp design** to include Parquet file-level `key_value_metadata` (per `_research/r6-pme-extraction-time-2026-05-17.md` R1+R7). Plan §2.3 D-NEW-D currently says `_extracted_at` recorded in `ParquetSnapshotRegistry.CreatedAt` only — INSUFFICIENT per user hard requirement "tell when raw data was extracted from source." Self-describing Parquet file (immutable post-write, survives DC-loss, 7-year retention may outlive registry row) requires file-level metadata. Recommended schema (R7): `udm_source_system` / `udm_source_schema` / `udm_source_table` / `udm_extraction_started_at` / `udm_extraction_ended_at` / `udm_parquet_written_at` / `udm_pipeline_batch_id` / `udm_pipeline_version` / `udm_encryption_config` / `udm_row_count`. Plus 2 new ParquetSnapshotRegistry columns (`ExtractionQueryStartedAt` + `ExtractionQueryCompletedAt`) per D92 forward-only ALTER for SQL-queryable index. **Gates Phase A** (extraction-timestamp is Phase A scope). Source: design-reviewer Section A + researcher R1+R7 convergence 2026-05-17.

- **B-357** (🟡 Open; **CRITICAL**; WSJF 5.0): **Fix `PiiSubjectKeys.SubjectIdentifier NVARCHAR(MAX)` DDL bug** — cannot be uniquely indexed in SQL Server (900-byte max key; NVARCHAR(MAX) not indexable). Change DDL to `SubjectPersonHash VARCHAR(64)` (SHA-256 hex per B-1 hash discipline) + corresponding UNIQUE INDEX. Add `SubjectKeyVersion INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 1` column for master-KEK rotation tracking (per `_research/r6-pme-extraction-time-2026-05-17.md` recommendation for D-NEW-E). **Gate-blocker for D-NEW-E lock**; Phase B scope. Source: design-reviewer F7 + researcher R-B5 convergence 2026-05-17.

- **B-358** (🟡 Open; HIGH; WSJF 4.0): **Specify PME-EC1 subject-key-generation HOLDLOCK pattern** in `pii_subject_keys.py` spec — must use `MERGE WITH (HOLDLOCK)` or try/catch-then-relookup pattern (per I3 anti-pattern guidance), NOT lookup-then-INSERT (race condition under concurrent extractors observing same subject). Phase B scope. Source: design-reviewer Section D PME-EC1 2026-05-17.

- **B-359** (🟡 Open; HIGH; WSJF 2.5): **Decide SubjectIdentifier granularity** (PME-EC3): person-scoped (e.g., hash of CustomerID for cross-table shred propagation) vs row-scoped (hash of table+PK). Determines `PiiSubjectKeys` schema — UNIQUE on `(SubjectPersonHash)` (person-scoped) vs `(TableName, RowKey)` (row-scoped) vs composite `(SubjectPersonHash, TableName)`. Recommendation per design-reviewer: person-scoped enables single-operation CCPA shredding covering all tables; row-scoped requires per-table enumeration without cross-table mapping (which doesn't exist in current design). Document cross-table shredding implications. **Gate-blocker for D-NEW-E DDL finalization**; Phase B scope. Source: design-reviewer Section D PME-EC3 2026-05-17.

- **B-360** (🟡 Open; HIGH; WSJF 1.67): **Extend CCPA-deletion SP per RB-10 `ProcProcessCcpaDeletion` for single-transaction crypto-shred + B-4 orphan sweep**: BEGIN TRAN + UPDATE PiiSubjectKeys SET EncryptedSubjectKey=NULL + INSERT PiiSubjectKeyShredLog + flip vault token Status='deleted_per_request' per existing RB-10 + subject-specific Bronze orphan force-close + COMMIT. Closes data-residue gap: crypto-shredded PME key makes Parquet rows unreadable but Bronze orphan rows (UdmActiveFlag=0 crash-orphans) may still reference valid vault tokens for the shredded subject. CCPA-deletion SP per RB-10 single-transaction atomicity required (preserves NORTH_STAR Pillar 1 audit-grade). Phase B scope (depends on B-357 + B-359 schema decisions). Source: design-reviewer Section C5 BLOCK 2026-05-17.

Phase B scope (depends on PME enabled). Source: design-reviewer Section D PME-EC2 + gap-check G6 finding 1 convergence 2026-05-17.

- **B-367** (🟡 Open; HIGH; WSJF 4.0): **Document SQL Server DATETIME2(7) → Parquet timestamp[us] precision loss** as accepted SE-2 exception. SQL Server DATETIME2(7) is 100-nanosecond precision; Parquet timestamp[us] is 1-microsecond precision; factor-of-10 truncation. Add `coerce_timestamps='us', allow_truncated_timestamps=True` to pyarrow write_table call with comment explaining tradeoff. Without explicit handling, pyarrow raises truncation exception. Add to `CLAUDE_GOTCHAS.md` as documented Polars/Arrow type-mapping caveat. Phase A scope (extraction layer is Phase A scope). Source: researcher R6-3 2026-05-17.

Required path (Option A per researcher R5): pipeline decrypts PME columns + tokenizes in-memory + COPY tokenized data to Snowflake; Snowflake receives tokens, NOT PME ciphertext. - **B-280** (🟡 Open): **HANDOFF §8 Pitfall #9.l sub-pattern — verbatim-extraction-safety against rendering-pipeline escape-collapse** — Surfaced 2026-05-15 by udm-gap-check independent reviewer (D.5 trim audit; G3+G6 finding 4). Discovered during D.5 verbatim extraction of B-6 Gotcha line from CLAUDE.md L467 → CLAUDE_GOTCHAS.md L48: the original line contained ` ` and ` ` escape-syntax representations of Unicode LINE SEPARATOR + PARAGRAPH SEPARATOR (the exact chars B-6 warns about as BCP-row-boundary-corrupting). When parent agent's `Write` tool rendered the file, the markdown-rendering pipeline COLLAPSED ` `/` ` escape sequences into LITERAL U+2028/U+2029 control characters — **introducing exactly the corruption B-6 documents the codebase avoiding**. Gap-check reviewer caught + fixed via PowerShell byte-level replacement. This is a 1st-event instance of a new Pitfall #9.l sub-pattern: rendering-pipeline-escape-collapse during verbatim text extraction. **Recommended discipline**: for any future verbatim extraction of content with control-character escape sequences, use `git show HEAD:<path> | sed -n 'X,Yp' > target` (preserves byte-exact content) rather than re-typing through Write tool. **2-event accumulation pending** before HANDOFF §8 sub-class formalization per `udm-subclass-accumulator` convention. **WSJF 1.5** (COD 2 — closes meta-discipline gap; JS 2 — accumulation + formalization). - **B-263** (🟡 Open): **Round 5 § 5.1 spec wording — `tokenize_pii_columns` is "deterministic" not "idempotent"** — Tier 2 property test cohort 2026-05-14 Agent A surfaced: `phase1/05_tests.md` § 5.1 lists `tokenize_pii_columns` in the master idempotence (D15) property list `f(f(x)) == f(x)`. SP-1's actual contract is plaintext-as-input: feeding a token BACK as plaintext mints a FRESH token (deterministic on same input plaintext, but NOT idempotent — `f(f(plaintext)) = f(token) = different_token != token`). Agent A's `test_idempotence.py` correctly preserves the property test by using a `TestTokenizePiiColumnsContract` wrapper that re-feeds the SAME plaintext (not the produced token) — proving SP-1 is deterministic on the plaintext-input contract. Spec § 5.1 wording should clarify: "Idempotence (D15) — for transformations that take DataFrames in/out: `f(f(df)) == f(df)`. For SP-wrapped transforms like `tokenize_pii_columns`, the property is determinism on the same input plaintext, not strict `f(f(x))` idempotence — SP-1 mints fresh tokens for re-fed tokens by design." **WSJF 1.0** (COD 1 — spec clarification; JS 1 — single paragraph edit in `phase1/05_tests.md` § 5.1). Closure target: next round close-out. Source: udm-gap-check 2026-05-14 Tier 2 cohort.
- **B-262** (~~🟡 Open~~ ⚫ CLOSED): ~~**`data_load/row_hash.py::_normalize_for_hashing` NFC-before-Categorical-cast ordering bug — PRODUCTION FIX**~~ — Tier 2 property test cohort 2026-05-14 Agent B's `test_hash_categorical_matches_utf8_for_same_logical_values` surfaced via Hypothesis (canonical property-test value catching what unit tests cannot). Trigger: any Categorical column carrying a value that NFC-normalizes differently from its raw form OR that contains trailing whitespace (Hypothesis discovered `' '` single-space + `豈` CJK compat codepoint independently). Bug: `_normalize_for_hashing()` applies NFC + RTRIM only to `string_cols` (pl.Utf8/String dtype) at L113-127, THEN detects Categorical cols at L141 and casts them to Utf8 + adds to `string_cols`. The NFC/RTRIM normalization is SKIPPED for the Categorical-derived Utf8 cols — they get hashed raw. Result: same logical string value hashes DIFFERENTLY depending on whether it arrived as Categorical vs Utf8 — violates E-20 invariant "Categorical hashed by logical value not physical encoding". Failing hash sample: Utf8(`' '`) RTRIMs to `''` → hash `e3b0c44...` (SHA-256 of empty), Categorical(`' '`) cast to Utf8 → hash `36a9e7f1...` (SHA-256 of `' '`). E-20 covers physical-integer-encoding trap but NOT NFC-equivalence between Utf8 and Categorical inputs. Fix: re-order normalization in `_normalize_for_hashing()` to run AFTER all Categorical → Utf8 + Binary → hex casts, OR re-apply NFC/RTRIM to newly-promoted string_cols set after each cast. Tests: `tests/property/test_hash_stability.py::test_hash_categorical_matches_utf8_for_same_logical_values` regresses deterministically once Hypothesis caches the counter-example (current state). Add E-20 docstring extension noting NFC equivalence post-fix. **WSJF 2.5** (COD 5 — real production hash-determinism bug affecting international PII / trailing-whitespace data; security-adjacent because affects hash chain integrity; JS 2 — single-function fix in `data_load/row_hash.py` + verification rerun + E-20 docstring touch). Closure target: next bug-fix cycle. Source: udm-gap-check 2026-05-14 Tier 2 cohort (independent reviewer verified via row_hash.py L113-141 read + isolated pytest reproduction). — ⚫ **CLOSED 2026-05-14** via NFC-before-Categorical-cast ordering fix in `data_load/row_hash.py::_normalize_for_hashing` (cast Categorical → Utf8 + Binary → hex BEFORE NFC/RTRIM normalization; re-detect string_cols after casts so unified set is normalized uniformly). Tier 1 regression backfill: 2 new tests in `tests/unit/test_hash_determinism.py` (`test_categorical_column_hashes_match_utf8_for_cjk_compat_codepoint` + `test_categorical_column_hashes_match_utf8_for_trailing_whitespace`) pinning Hypothesis-discovered counter-examples. Tier 1 ↔ Tier 2 feedback loop operationalized. Full pytest: 1985 pass / 14 skip / 2 fail (0 new regression vs 1983/14/2 baseline). See `_validation_log.md` 2026-05-14 entry "B-262 production bug fix + Tier 1 regression backfill + tracker cleanup (gap-audit 4 findings closed)".

- **B-254** (🟡 Open): **M3 `parquet_registry_client.list_snapshots()` helper extraction — Round 4.1 § 3.1 `tools/parquet_tier_review.py` producer audit 2026-05-14**. Round 4.1 § 3.1 build (Round 4 cohort 1st of 5; 1,464 lines; 71 tests pass; 0 inline cycles) surfaced an M3 API gap: § 3.1 needs to walk multiple `ParquetSnapshotRegistry` rows filtered by `(status, age_days, source, table)` for the status-transition review, but the existing canonical M3 surface `query_snapshot()` returns a single row by exact key (per Round 3 § 1.3 spec). § 3.1 currently composes M3 via direct cursor reads against `ParquetSnapshotRegistry` to walk the filter — bypassing M3 idiom + duplicating query-construction code. **Migration plan**: extract `list_snapshots(*, status: str | None = None, age_days: int | None = None, source: str | None = None, table: str | None = None, limit: int = 1000) -> list[ParquetSnapshot]` helper into `data_load/parquet_registry_client.py` (M3). § 3.1 then composes the helper instead of direct cursor reads. - **B-246** (🟡 Open): **I20 hash-version migration column — `HashVersion VARCHAR(20)` on `ParquetSnapshotRegistry` + `IdempotencyLedger` DDLs** — I20 edge-case sweep surfaced gap: when the project's hash algorithm evolves (e.g. SHA-256 → SHA3-256 if SHA-256 is ever deprecated, or hash-input-normalization changes per W-2 / W-3 / E-1 / E-4 / E-20 evolution), there is no per-row version tag to distinguish "legacy hash" rows from "current hash" rows. Cross-version comparison (e.g. verify-replay against an older `ContentChecksum` value after a hash algorithm change) would silently produce false-mismatch verdicts. **Migration plan**: (a) ALTER `General.ops.ParquetSnapshotRegistry` ADD `HashVersion VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'sha256-1'`; (b) ALTER `General.ops.IdempotencyLedger` ADD `HashVersion VARCHAR(20) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'sha256-1'`; (c) CHECK constraint on both tables: `HashVersion IN ('sha256-1', 'sha256-2', ...)` with an explicit canonical-list of supported versions; (d) at verify/replay time, reject cross-version comparison via raise (don't silently coerce). Forward-only additive per D92 — additive ALTER + SchemaContract row + canonical-value-list enumeration. **Closure target**: Round 6 schema-evolution governance OR Round 5 Tier 3 (Tests / scale-validation phase). **WSJF 1.5** (COD 3 — future-proofing for hash-algorithm evolution + audit-grade discriminator; JS 2 — 2 ALTERs + 2 CHECK constraints + raise-path branch in verify/replay + SchemaContract row). - **B-235** (🟡 Open): **M5 SP-2 disambiguation enhancement — SP-2 should return 1 row with `PlaintextValue=NULL` for `deleted_per_request` / `purged_for_retention` token statuses** — `data_load/pii_decryptor.py::decrypt_token()` currently treats SP-2 (`PiiVault_DecryptForOperator`) returning 0 rows as `TokenNotFound`. However, SP-2 implementation also returns 0 rows when the token IS present but has been excluded due to CCPA-deletion (`deleted_per_request`) or retention purge (`purged_for_retention`) — meaning M5 cannot distinguish "no such token" from "token deleted; decrypt forbidden". **Migration plan**: extend SP-2 to return 1 row with `(Token, PlaintextValue=NULL, ExclusionReason)` for excluded-status tokens; M5 then raises `DecryptDenied(reason=ExclusionReason)` instead of `TokenNotFound`. **Closure target**: Round 1 SP-2 revision (forward-only additive per D92 — append OUTPUT column) OR Round 7 schema-evolution governance (SchemaContract row + dual-rev rollout). **WSJF 1.5** (COD 3 — audit-grade signal for CCPA-deleted access attempts; JS 2 — SP body update + M5 raise-path branch + Tier 1 tests). - **B-234** (🟡 Open): **M4 per-column PiiType mapping — Round 3 § 2.1 spec does not define the per-column PiiType source; M4 defaults to OTHER** — `data_load/pii_tokenizer.py::tokenize_pii_columns()` per the spec accepts `column_list: list[str]` of PII column names but does NOT receive per-column `PiiType` (SSN / EMAIL / PHONE / ADDRESS / OTHER) which SP-1 requires for category-aware tokenization. M4 currently defaults to `PiiType=OTHER` for every column — undermining downstream policy-aware reporting (e.g. "decrypt count by SSN vs EMAIL"). **Migration plan**: (a) ADD `PiiType` column to `UdmTablesColumnsList` (additive per D92 + SchemaContract row); (b) `tokenize_pii_columns()` reads `PiiType` per column from `UdmTablesColumnsList` query; (c) document the mapping in spec § 2.1. - **B-233** (🟡 Open): **M1 UncompressedBytes = file_size_bytes (compressed) placeholder** — `data_load/parquet_writer.py::write_parquet_snapshot()` populates `ParquetSnapshotRegistry.UncompressedBytes` with the compressed file size (`Path.stat().st_size`) as a placeholder. - **B-232** (🟡 Open): **M1 SchemaHash / ContentChecksum both = full file SHA-256 (placeholder)** — `data_load/parquet_writer.py::write_parquet_snapshot()` populates `ParquetSnapshotRegistry.SchemaHash` AND `ParquetSnapshotRegistry.ContentChecksum` with the same full file SHA-256 hex digest. Future enhancement: distinguish a schema-only fingerprint (e.g. canonical-form digest of the Parquet schema columns / types / Hive partition columns) from the content checksum (full file SHA-256 stays). This unlocks downstream "schema drift" detection at the registry level — two files with identical SchemaHash but different ContentChecksum = pure data change; mismatched SchemaHash = upstream schema evolution event. **Migration plan**: author `utils/parquet_metadata.py::compute_schema_hash(path)` reading `pyarrow.parquet.read_schema(path)` -> canonical-form string -> SHA-256; M1 calls it post-write. - **B-225** (🟡 Open): **`SensitiveDataFilter` does not redact `record.exc_info` — `logger.exception()` traceback leak** — M14 / `observability/sensitive_data_filter.py::SensitiveDataFilter.filter()` redacts `record.msg` + `record.args` but does NOT process `record.exc_info` (the `(type, value, traceback)` tuple Python attaches when `logger.exception()` is called inside `except`). If an exception message contains plaintext credentials (e.g. `raise ConnectionError("auth failed with password=topsecret")`), the formatted traceback in `PipelineLog` will leak the password. This is a **P5 (no plaintext PII anywhere in logs) violation surface**. Spec § 6.1 doesn't address `exc_info` explicitly — gap-check 2026-05-13 surfaced. **Migration plan**: extend `SensitiveDataFilter.filter()` to (a) walk `record.exc_info` tuple if present; (b) apply `_redact()` to `str(exc_value)`; (c) optionally walk traceback frames for local-variable leakage (advanced). Path (a)+(b) covers the canonical case (most plaintext leaks via `str(exc)`); path (c) is defense-in-depth. **Closure target**: Round 5 (Tests phase) when broader P5 audit drill runs; OR sooner if any module starts using `logger.exception()` with credential-adjacent code. **WSJF 1.5** (COD 3 — P5 violation surface; JS 2 — filter() extension + Tier 1 parametrized exc_info tests). Source: udm-gap-check 2026-05-13 (independent reviewer per CLAUDE.md hard rule 11).

- **B197** (🟡 Open): **RB-14 SELinux `semanage fcontext` step addition** — Pattern E R1C1-5 advisory researcher 2026-05-12 found that RB-14's `restorecon -v /etc/pipeline/.env` step alone is insufficient for the custom non-standard path `/etc/pipeline/.env`. RHEL canonical guidance (Red Hat RHEL 6/7/9 practitioner docs + "Four semanage commands to keep SELinux in enforcing mode") requires `semanage fcontext -a -t <type> "/etc/pipeline(/.*)?"` FIRST to register the file-context policy rule, THEN `restorecon -Rv /etc/pipeline/` resolves to the correct service-confining type. Without the first step, the file gets generic `etc_t` label rather than correct service-specific confinement — silently breaking D103 Layer 11 (SELinux enforcing). **R1 acceptance depends on this fix**: Phase 2 R1 § 4.1 delegates to RB-14; if RB-14 has the SELinux gap, R1's SELinux assurance is illusory. **Procedure**: sysadmin confirms the correct SELinux type (likely a custom `pipeline_config_t` type per project-specific policy module OR documented use of `etc_t` if acceptable); update RB-14 § procedure to include `semanage fcontext` step BEFORE `restorecon`; re-run validation on dev → test → prod. **Author location**: edit `05_RUNBOOKS.md` RB-14 § 5.2 procedure (per D92 forward-only — RB-14 is locked but additive procedure addition is permitted; SchemaContract pattern doesn't apply to runbooks but D93 cross-doc cascade does). **Hard prerequisite for R1 § 4.1 acceptance** — flagged as 🔴-class blocking item. **WSJF 4.0** (COD 8 — directly affects D103 security model assurance; JS 2 — sysadmin coordination + RB-14 edit + per-server re-verification). Surfaces 2026-05-12 via Pattern E R1C1-5; needs sysadmin input on canonical SELinux type before edit.
